Round 14 feature match - Brandon Burton vs. Brian Six
-----------------------------------------------------


*by Duncan McGregor*

At 11-2 going into the round, the winner of this match still wasn't guaranteed a berth in the Top 8, but the loser would definitely be out. While neither of them is a household name yet, both are experienced players. Brian narrowly missed another Top 8 earlier this year, finishing 10th at Grand Prix-Los Angeles, and also moneyed Pro Tour-Berlin last year. Brandon, who is in a wheelchair as a result of a medical condition, plays a lot of **Magic Online**, as sandydogmtg - a common name to see at the top of the standings. His mother Elizabeth was in attendance with him today to help him out, but the playing and the decisions were all Brandon.


Brian won the die roll, but had to mulligan once to find a keepable hand. He fetched a [Taiga](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Taiga) for his [Kird Ape](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kird+Ape), then a [Plateau](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plateau) on his second turn for [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf). Brandon had started his game with [Mutavault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mutavault) for [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=%C3%86ther+Vial), then [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland)ed Brian's [Taiga](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Taiga) on his second turn. Brian had no more land and swung in with his pair of one-power creatures. A [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Aether%2BVial)ed in [Cursecatcher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cursecatcher) drew a [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) before blockers, though, levelling up ‘Goyf. Brian passed the turn ahead on life 18-14.


Brandon put his [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Aether%2BVial) up to 2, then played a [Silvergill Adept](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silvergill+Adept), telegraphing a [Lord of Atlantis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lord+of+Atlantis). Brian swung back again with [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) before playing a fresh [Bloodstained Mire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodstained+Mire) to replace his fallen [Taiga](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Taiga). He threw a [Grim Lavamancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grim+Lavamancer) and a [Rift Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rift+Bolt) out before passing. Brandon [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Aether%2BVial)ed in the Lord at end of turn, and when his [Silvergill Adept](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silvergill+Adept) went unblocked he [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Aether%2BVial)ed in another one to knock Brian to 13. Brandon then [Stifle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stifle)d the [Rift Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rift+Bolt)'s trigger the next turn when the last time counter came off, keeping it from ever resolving and leaving them two cards in hand each.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/FM14_Six.jpg)*Brian Six is a prominent fixture on the Grand Prix scene...*Brian swung in with [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) and [Kird Ape](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kird+Ape). Brandon blocked the Ape with one Lord, falling to 8 from the [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), and then had a second [Stifle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stifle) ready when Brian tried to Lavamancer the wounded Lord. Brian thought about his options, and finally floated his other mana as [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze) protection before sacrificing both his land to Fireblast the other Lord. This removed both Lords from the table, but left Brian no sources of mana for his Lavamancer - a failing that Brandon was ready to exploit with a [Wake Thrasher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wake+Thrasher). Brian did not draw land on his next turn, and Brandon tapped his Æther [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Aether%2BVial) and activated [Mutavault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mutavault) with his remaining mana to make [Wake Thrasher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wake+Thrasher) a 7/7. The big fish smashed Brian down to 3, and was joined by a second one. Brian drew a land on his next turn, but it was too late by then.


Brandon 1 - 0 Brian


Brandon commented between games that the matchup was very bad for him, and it became even more so when he had to mulligan to 5 in Game 2. He was able to [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) a [Grim Lavamancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grim+Lavamancer) and [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) a [Taiga](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Taiga) to keep a [Kird Ape](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kird+Ape) small, but Brian returned the favor with [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) on a [Mutavault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mutavault). Another fetchland off the top for a new [Taiga](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Taiga) turned [Kird Ape](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kird+Ape) back on and allowed a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), and Brandon, still with no action, packed it in to save time for Game 3.


Brandon 1 - 1 Brian


Brandon led with Æther [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Aether%2BVial), while Brian - fearing [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) - fetched only a [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain) to suspend [Rift Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rift+Bolt). Brandon proved that paranoids can have enemies too, playing a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) before passing. [Rift Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rift+Bolt) went to the dome, and Brian played [Windswept Heath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Windswept+Heath) and suspended another [Rift Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rift+Bolt). Brandon tossed [Cursecatcher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cursecatcher) into play during his end step, then played another [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) and attacked. Brian chose to [Rift Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rift+Bolt) the [Cursecatcher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cursecatcher), then passed the turn without any other plays.


Brandon used [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Aether%2BVial) to drop [Lord of Atlantis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lord+of+Atlantis) into play, also playing an [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) before passing. Brian sent out for a [Plateau](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plateau) during his end step, which was promptly [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland)ed, but Brian used the mana to send a [Magma Jet](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Magma+Jet) at [Lord of Atlantis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lord+of+Atlantis). Brandon hard-cast a [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze) to stop that. Brian looked somewhat nonplussed at that, but while he didn't have any board position he did have six cards in hand to Brandon's two - if he ever got the land to use them. He elected to use his one [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain) to Chain Lightning the Lord, but Brandon continued to have answers, in the form of [Hydroblast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hydroblast).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/FM14_Burton.jpg)*...while Brandon Burton is a Magic Online powerhouse.*Brandon drew another question on his next turn, dropping [Wake Thrasher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wake+Thrasher) into play, but with a [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain) off the top Brian had enough mana for a [Pyroclasm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pyroclasm), and Brandon's team was sent to the graveyard. Brandon tried to refuel with a [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Aether%2BVial)ed out [Silvergill Adept](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silvergill+Adept) but only found another [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=%C3%86ther+Vial), while Brian resolved a [Grim Lavamancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grim+Lavamancer). The [Silvergill Adept](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silvergill+Adept) hit Brian again to knock him to 11, but a third [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Aether%2BVial) was not what Brandon was looking for. With the Lavamancer active Brian offed the lone merfolk and then started aiming burn directly at Brandon. A [Taiga](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Taiga) was quickly [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland)ed, meaning that the [Wild Nacatl](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wild+Nacatl) Brian played was only 1/1, but Brandon didn't have any answers for it, or for the Lavamancer, or the burn that Brian sent his way.


Brian Six defeats Brandon Burton 2-1.


  


Sunday 2:40 p.m. - Quick Judge Hits
-----------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

What was your most memorable Magic situation of the weekend?


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/John-Aldorfer.jpg)John Aldorver: Watching a player successfully stack their deck in a minute after resolving Charbelcher.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Ingrid-Lind-Jahn.jpg)Ingrid Lind-Jahn: I answered a question about [Humility](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Humility) while two judges in a row were doing it too. It was a [Humility](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Humility) zone. Two were even the same question.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Josh-Schroeder.jpg)Josh Schroeder: The Legacy format has a number of interactions and rules that it provokes that was more than I expected. And I was impressed with a lot of the players who were able to explain rules just like a judge would.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/James-Hooker.jpg)James Hooker: The overwhelming fact that this was a huge, massive event and we got it done in a reasonable amount of time.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/William-Colley.jpg)William Colley: I wrote a 1 ½ minute time extension for rain. It was actually raining on their match.


  


Round 15 Feature Match: Gabriel Nassif vs. Josh Utter-Leyton
------------------------------------------------------------


*by Bill Stark*

“Do you need to qualify for Hawaii?” French player Gabriel Nassif asked his opponent as he sat down to the Round 15 feature match.


“Yeah,” Josh Utter-Leyton responded, squashing any hopes Gabriel might have had for a concession to sneak the Pro Tour-Kyoto champion into the Top 8. The American, who goes by “Wrapter” amongst his friends, is associated with the large contingent of players who work alongside Luis Scott-Vargas. He won the die roll, and watched quietly as his opponent opted to take a mulligan.


[Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) hit the board for Utter-Leyton on his second turn, and immediately yielded advantages, flipping a blind two-drop to counter Gabriel Nassif's efforts at a second-turn [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf). When Josh followed the play up with a [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top), Gabriel looked a bit disappointed. Still, his long and illustrious professional career didn't come on the back of giving up in tough situations, and he made a [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) in an attempt to answer the ‘Goyf. Josh cashed his Divining Top in, revealing it to [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) and countering the removal spell.


But it was a ruse! Nassif actually wanted to stick a [Sower of Temptation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sower+of+Temptation), which he did on his own turn, stealing the [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf). By feinting Josh into being concerned about the Swords, Gabriel had managed to set up a situation in which he could potentially steal the game!


Josh was having none of it, however. He untapped, played a Swords of his own targeting the [Sower of Temptation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sower+of+Temptation), and wresting control of the game back. Rather than try to claw his way in under now insurmountable odds, Nassif conceded.


Josh Utter-Leyton 1, Gabriel Nassif 0


[Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) was the first creature on the board in the second game, joining the table for Gabriel Nassif with nary a peep from Josh Utter-Leyton. To his credit, Josh followed it right up with a [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant), but Nassif had the [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) to kill the troublesome Wizard. Utter-Leyton dug for more action with [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/FM15_Nassif.jpg)*Can Nassif make it back-to-back Top 8s?*
Nassif missed a land drop, but was on a beat down path with his early game [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf). He took a long pause to consider allowing Josh to resolve a [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top), but ultimately opted to use [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) to counter the artifact. His draw failed to yield a land, and he simply attacked to put the score 17-16 in his favor. Trying to start an offense himself, Josh played a [Trygon Predator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trygon+Predator), but considering his opponent's board had neither artifacts nor enchantments, the card was merely a 2/3.


Still there was no land for Gabriel Nassif, but he had drawn a strew of [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will)s, and could actually sit back for a game of aggro-control, letting his [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) do the walking while his counterspells did the talking. By the time he finally hit the third land, he was able to play [Trygon Predator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trygon+Predator). That resolved successfully, but a second was countered from a lucky [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) reveal by Utter-Leyton one turn later. The Californian had successfully resolved the enchantment with no disruption from his opponent.


Josh was falling behind, on increasingly lower and lower life. He attempted to play more chump blockers, but Nassif decided to pull the trigger on his counterspells. He used [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) to prevent a [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) from hitting play, and Josh turned to [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) for some help. The *Coldsnap* standout failed to yield him the five-drop he needed to counter the counter and, at 2 life facing down a [Trygon Predator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trygon+Predator) and [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) with no solutions, he conceded.


Josh Utter-Leyton 1, Gabriel Nassif 1


It was Josh Utter-Leyton's turn to mulligan for the third game of the match, but he quickly regained the disadvantage by playing a first-turn [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top). The little artifact would provide him plenty of gas to make up for starting down a card, and he even had a [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze) to counter his opponent's attempt to play a Top of his own on the first turn.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/FM15_ULeyton.jpg)*Josh Utter-Leyton takes a turn in the Feature Match spotlight.*
The two players continued trying to mirror one another as Nassif played a second-turn [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) which was matched by one from Josh. The players finally took divergent paths, when Nassif was able to stick a second [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) alongside a [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance), while Josh missed a land drop. That series of events spelled very bad news for Josh Utter-Leyton, who was left facing increasingly insurmountable odds. [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) for Gabe as well as the [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance)/Top lock; by the time Nassif was attempting to resolve [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) it seemed all but over.


That said, it *wasn't* over, not just yet. Josh used a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) to counter the [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), but Nassif simply nodded, played his land for the turn, and cast a second copy of the card. Utter-Leyton spun his Top in response, trying to find a second counter, but whiffed. He did have a [Trygon Predator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trygon+Predator) to potentially block, but he was unaware that Nassif was slowrolling a [Vedalken Shackles](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vedalken+Shackles) he could play and use to steal the 2/3 all in one turn.


That's exactly what he did, turning both his [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) and [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) sideways to the red zone and putting Josh to an interesting conundrum. Should he trade his [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) for Nassif's, or hold the 2/1 a bit longer hoping the extra cards could bring him out of his predicament? He took the damage, falling to 7 and in worse and worse shape. Now he had to deal with the [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance)/Top lock, [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant), and his own [Trygon Predator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trygon+Predator) attacking him!


When Nassif attempted to activate his [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) at the end of the turn, Josh responded with [Krosan Grip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krosan+Grip) targeting [Vedalken Shackles](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vedalken+Shackles). That got him his Predator back, but not for long. Nassif simply untapped and played [Sower of Temptation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sower+of+Temptation) to steal the 2/3 right back, then bashed in again with [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) and [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant). This time Josh chumped the ‘Goyf and fell to 5. With the turn back, he untapped, cashed in his Top for a free card, found no help and was forced to concede the game.


Gabriel Nassif 2, Josh Utter-Leyton 1
